O you, dear sons, I have completed this book for you which contains the principles and the fullness of the medical sciences, and have ended it with explanations and clarifications. And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is, "surgery."
And because the practice of surgery is forbidden in our region and is banned everywhere, the science has perished and been cut off, and nothing remains of it except for small descriptions in books by ancient authors which have been handled by hands. And because of this, errors and falsehoods have arisen, and understanding has been closed off and the science has been driven away.
It seems to me that I wish to compile together the organization of this treatise following the order of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will compile together the forms of the fire-making tools for cautery, as well as the other instruments of the craft with the addition of explanation and preparation as is necessary.
And because no skilled craftsmen of the hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has declined. And it is necessary for one who practices (medicine) to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that they know precisely about the members, their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of the bones and nerves and veins and the number of arteries, and their movement and repose, and where they originate.
And so Hippocrates said that the name is much with the name, and little with the work; and it is the same in the art of hands. (Meaning that the reputation or name of a surgeon or physician may be great, but their actual skills and abilities are what truly matter)
We tell you at the beginning of this book, that whoever is not knowledgeable about the previously mentioned things, should be careful not to fall into error and not to kill men; as I have seen many times with those who meddle in this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and experience.
For I saw a foolish surgeon who lanced an abscess of scrofula on a woman's neck and cut the arteries of the neck, so that so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in her hands.
And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone in a man's bladder, and the stone was large, and he removed a piece of the bladder along with it, and the man died within three days.
And I had already been called to see him (the patient) and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew well that if he operated on him, he would die.
And see one other doctor who took in charge a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break, there was a wound; and the ignorant doctor tightly binds the break over the wound with splints, and did not leave any bandage at the wound, and he left it like this for a while; and he ordered him not to loosen it; and it remained so until the leg became swollen and the foot became gangrenous.
I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and unbind his leg; and when I had undone it, he was calm and felt no pain.
But in any case, the corruption had already set in the limb, and I could not heal it; and the corruption continued to spread through the limb until it was completely lost.
And see one other doctor who ruptured an enlarged abscess, and then inflamed it further through the malice of his treatment.
Because when a chancre is pure of melancholic humor, it should not be touched with iron unless it is in such a place that all corrupt matter can be completely removed.
And so, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: that is, work where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will point out in every part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to be cautious, so that foolish fools cannot speak ill of you.
Take up your weapons in cotton (gauze), and approach your patients lightly and steadily, and use the best method so that through the grace of God you may come to safety and be praised; and leave behind the diseases that inspire dread with serious illness; and put away your weapons from those that make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galen says in one of his admonitions: "Do not take care of serious illness, for you will be called a foolish fool."
I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
The first chapter is about cauteries of fire and medical caustics, and this chapter is arranged from head to toe; and the forms of instruments, and the iron tools for cauterization, and all that is necessary for the work.
The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping glasses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is arranged and includes the forms of instruments.[](https://french.stackexchange.com/)
The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and sprains, and similar conditions, and it covers the entire body from head to toe, as well as the forms of instruments. This passage indicates that the chapter provides instructions for treating injuries such as dislocated joints and twisted limbs using surgical tools.
So that we may remember the work, it is necessary for me to describe the qualities of care and the harmfulness of each temperament. This passage suggests that the text will discuss how different bodily temperaments (e.g., sanguine, phlegmatic) respond to medical treatment and the potential risks associated with treating patients of certain temperaments.[2](https://french.stackexchange.com/a/50136)
I say that the qualities of help, and harm, are the longest in word and the most subtle in science and hidden knowledge; and of this, many sages spoke and agreed to it; and I am not satisfied with their words, because I fear their length.
I say that the cautery helps universally for all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, the hot complexion without matter, and the dry complexion without matter.
In the hot and dry complexion together with matter, some have divided and said that the cautery is of great help there; and others have said the opposite: that the cautery is not worth anything for the illness that comes from heat and dryness.
For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to cure a disease caused by heat and dryness; and those who say the opposite claim that the cautery provides great help for a hot and dry illness that arises in the body of humans. For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body to be cold.
And I agree with this statement. For I have found it to be true through experience.
And yet, it should not be meddled with by anyone other than the one who has experienced it and is knowledgeable about the chapter of cauteries, as well as the diversity of human complexions, dispositions, and causes of their illnesses, and their outcomes and the season; we are not afraid of other complexions, even those that are cold and moist. And all the physicians gathered together and agreed on the use of the cautery.
And know, son, that a fire cautery is also one of the surgical instruments of treatments, and of greater virtue than a caustic medical cautery.
For fire is simple and does not spread beyond the member that is burned, and does not harm any other member unless it happens to do so.
Caustic medical substances spread from one member to another and bring sickness with severe consequences to the affected member; and perhaps kill the patient.

And this I have found through experience and the length of time spent in service and studying the art, and it is based on the truth of things; and therefore I excuse myself for the length of my speech, for it does not please me to take away from you the secret that is hidden within fire, and its quality of work, how it drives out illnesses from bodies, as philosophers have said in their demonstrations. Now receive this in your thoughts.
And know, son, that they agreed on what time cauteries should be performed, and chose priests.
And I say that a cautery is appropriate in all cases, because harmful effects arising from it are minimized by the use of the cautery; and similarly, even if cauterization causes pain, it is necessary to perform quickly without delay, before greater harm comes to the member.
And never think, dear son, as foolish people do; for a disease healed by cauterization does not return, and they say so; but it is not what they think, because a cautery is not merely a medicine that changes the complexion, but rather it dries up the humors that cause pain, and works more quickly than other medicines due to its power and authority.
It is possible that a disease may come at times according to the complexion of the patient and the location and nature of the disease; and excessive fluids accumulate in him due to the consumption of foods and similar things, unless cauteries are administered where there is little excess fluid and moisture, such as cauterization with hot irons for pain, and similar things. In this case, the pain does not return, but it happens infrequently.
And many people do not understand why cautery is called the "last resort" of medicine, but this is indeed the case; however, they do not believe that cautery can be effective after other treatments, but their belief is false. The reason cautery is called the "last resort" of medicine is because when we administer methods of cure for a disease and they are not effective, we then administer cauterization, and it is effective. Then it becomes clear that cautery is the "last resort" of medicine, and not in the way foolish doctors think.
The ancients said that cautery with an instrument of gold is more gentle than iron, and they only said this because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance. They also said that the place of cauterization does not cause gangrene, but this is not true as I have experienced. However, they were correct in saying that gold cautery is more effective than iron, just as they claimed.
And yet, when heating an instrument of gold, you cannot be sure when it is hot enough because the color of gold does not change much, and it can quickly cool down again. Additionally, if it is heated too much, it may become brittle and break in the fire. Thus, there are many difficulties with using a gold cautery instrument.[/] The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
And so we make use of the fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
I have arranged this chapter on wounds from head to toe, so that the way may be easier to find.
olive cautery (referring to a type of cauterization)
This cautery is good for moistness and coldness in the brain, and there are two types that are made for a disease called "soda" (possibly epilepsy) and for many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for an abundance of dreams, pain in the teeth and throat, and also for all illnesses that come from coldness, such as paralysis and numbness and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
The form of this cautery is that the patient must be purged with a cleansing medicine, clearing the head for three or four nights, depending on what the virtues (strength), water and habits of the patient can bear; and then heat up the patient's head.[Source](https://www.perseus.tufts.edu/hopper/text?doc=Perseus%3Atext%3A2007.04.0059%3Asid%3D186)
And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on something heavy; then place the base of your palm on the base of his nose between his two eyes; and where your middle fingers come, bleed a little and then heat the cautery called "olivare," which looks like this:
And place it on the mark made with ink, and make a small wound while pulling downward and outward with your hand; then quickly remove your hand and look at the mark to see if you see a hole as small as a pin; and if you do not see it, reapply the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; then take a little bit of salt and put it in warm water and soft cotton, and place it on the mark and leave it for three days; then apply a wet cloth soaked in butter and leave it on until the heat is gone; then treat the wound with the "tetrafarmaçon" ointment until it heals.
And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges; and because of this, movement helps.
And some of them said that one should let the cautery burn long enough that a part of the bone is burnt, and then remove what has been burnt from the bone and have it treated.
And they say that one should leave the cautery for a while, and apply it strongly enough that it makes a hole as large as a buckle that women put in their shoes so that the humors may come out; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; after that, one should clean and close it.
And these two methods of cautery do not seem good to me at all, except in certain men where there is a cause for fear; and it seems to me that I should leave them; for the head is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we have witnessed in other members; and even when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more healing and powerful for me, and I use this one to bring about a cure.

The term "litargie" is a variant spelling of "litharge," which was a type of medicine made from lead oxide that was used in the Middle Ages to treat various conditions such as skin diseases, ulcers, and eye inflammations. It could be applied topically or taken internally. The exact recipe for making litharge varied, but it typically involved heating lead ore or lead metal with vinegar or another acid to create a powder or paste. Litharge was also known by other names such as "ceruse" and "lead white." However, the use of litharge in medicine declined over time due to concerns about its toxicity, particularly its potential to cause lead poisoning. Modern medical treatments no longer include litharge.

the hair that pricks the eye It sometimes happens that the eyelashes are turned inward and prick the eye, and in such cases cauteries are performed in two ways: with fire or with a heated medicinal substance.
For the fire cautery, the patient is instructed to let the eyelashes grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, to hold the eyes steady so that they do not move until they grow.
When they are born and even, then place the patient in your care; afterward, on a piece of paper place an image that is similar to the leaf of a fern, and let the beginning of the sign be next to the hairs; then put cotton soaked in egg white and powdered pearl on the eye, then heat the cautery to the shape described here:
After cauterizing the image you have marked many times, so that the flesh is burnt there; and the sign of the success of the work is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs raised at the edge of the eye; then lift your hand and leave it like that for three days, then put cotton soaked in butter on it until the burn is healed; after that, treat with ointment until it is healed.
And if after that the hairs grow back and the paper becomes soft again, then begin cauterizing in that same place as before; and if the hairs are missing, cauterize until the paper rises to its natural level, so that it is even and the hairs do not prick the eye.
The fiery medical cautery is what you command the patient to let their hairs grow long and even until they are large and even; then make a form from parchment in the shape of a fern leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each one third, and grind them well together; and do it quickly so that it does not cool; then spread it on the form you have made similar to the fern leaf, and place it on the paper of the eyes; and if the illness is in only one eye, then work on only one, and if in both as well; and put cotton soaked in egg white under the eye; and let the patient's head be in your care and place your hand over the medicine, and press a little and move it all the time that the patient feels the biting of the medicine, for they feel it like being burnt by fire. When you have done this for a long time, remove the medicine from its place. And when the biting (pain) has passed, lift the area of application and check if you see the skin raised as if it had been raised by constriction of fire or incision; and if it is so, then it is good. If not, apply more medicine to the area where the medicine has not worked, until your tasks are even and your eyes are healed; then place a wet cotton compress soaked in butter on the burnt area until the burn has cooled down. Afterwards, cure the site of the ointment application, which is called "dyafenis" and other names, until it is healed.
And if you need to be careful with your work and take great care that no medicine gets into the eyes. And if the skin becomes soft afterwards, and hairs prick at the eye, then reapply the medicine to the affected area, treating it properly as before; after that, cure it until it is healed. This is the form of the medical leaflet.[9]

of the treatment of fistula by cautery
When you treat a fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your treatments are not effective, then you should apply cautery to it in this manner.
Instruct the patient to place their head in your lap; and hold the patient's head steady between your hands so that it does not move or shift; then apply a cotton swab soaked with egg white or parsley juice on the eye; after that, heat up the cautery which is shaped like a pen nib, and place it on the head so that it touches the skin; if you wish, shape it to be pointed from one end to the other, or in the form of a tent; but in any case, this will be useful for your work.
Afterwards, press on the fistula if it is open, and remove any pus or debris from it; and if it is closed, then incise it and remove the contents; then apply hot flour to the cautery, and hold the cautery to the eye, being careful not to move your hand excessively; place the cautery in the fat of the eye, allowing it to melt and corrupt.
If you are able to reach the bone with the cautery at the beginning, that would be good. If not, then apply the cautery again, and continue doing so as many times as necessary, leaving it in place for three days; after that, apply a cotton swab soaked in butter to it, and treat the eye with a drying ointment until it heals; if 40 days pass and it is not healed, then use a corrosive medicine to uncover the bone; and treat the eye according to what is written in the appropriate chapter of the text.
And there is a type of cautery for a fistula that some of the ancients mentioned. Understand "fistula," and open the area; then place in the opening a thin piece of [something], the shape of which is as follows: And they make it to the size of a three-penny piece; and hold your hand firmly on the [something], and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted [something] does not run into his eye; and it is necessary to put raw cotton soaked in egg yolk or oil on the patient's eye: the [something] will draw out the area of the fistula, and the healthy flesh will heal miraculously.
And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we mentioned, it is good. If not, then one must administer pus to the newborn and return the fistula to the body of the newborn as it should be in its proper place.

of the abscess in the throat
When an abscess comes to the root of the throat or in the eye, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth, after it has rotted and turned and become a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, but it is not successful: then it is necessary that you have a cautery according to the size of the fistula; then apply the opening or hole of the fistula, and hold your hand until the hot iron reaches the bottom of it, and behind the wound; and do this once or twice, after the treatment that we have said in treatments, until it is healed; and if it is treated in this way, it is good; and if not, then you must uncover the place and remove the rotten bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
from movement of the teeth
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines but to no avail, then place the patient's head in your lap; after that, heat the cautery until it is glowing red, shaping it in such a way that you can place a stick on the tooth; and quickly insert the hot cautery, holding your hand in place until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand and reapply the cautery as you wish; after that, have the patient fill their mouth with salty water and gargle it for an hour.
And in this way, the moving tooth is stabilized, and the softened gum is constrained, and the moisture is dried up and corrupted.
of tooth pain
When tooth pain comes from coldness, whether real or imagined, and medical cures are ineffective, then it is necessary to use the cautery in two ways: with butter and with fire.
Cautery of butter is as follows: take cow's butter, and the tip in an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a tent (perhaps meaning a rod or stick), and moisten it in boiled butter, and place it on the painful tooth quickly and hold it until it has cooled down; and do this frequently until the virtue (heat) reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see (it is necessary) to moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the painful tooth, and place a hot iron on it until the heat reaches the base of the tooth.
The fire cautery is as follows: take an iron rod of iron or bronze, and make it thick enough so that the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, which will form as follows, and place it on the tooth while holding your hand until the cautery has cooled down; do this frequently, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next. And it is necessary that the patient fills their mouth with good butter in the haste of this cautery, and then spits it out; and this is the form of the cautery:
When the scrofulous swellings are due to phlegm and cold moistures, and are not responsive to digestion by medicines, then heat the fire-steel until it glows red, and make two openings for the fumes to escape on the side of the fire-brand; place the hot iron on the abscess once or twice as needed, until it reaches the base of the abscess; if the abscess is small, apply the iron according to its size, and leave it in place for three days; then apply a wet compress soaked in butter until the burn heals; after that, treat the area with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
When the moistures overcome the channels of the throat, and also when it is due to a cold complexion, then the patient should be purged first with resolvent medicines; after that, perform cautery at the base of the throat, but make sure not to burn the windpipe or the heart, only a little bit; then perform another cautery at the joint between the neck and the spine, using an iron shaped like a "clavicle," as we have described before; and treat the area as we have said before until it is healed.

Afterward, have the patient recline on their back and side; afterward, lift the heart that is within the chest with the tips of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery that has two nerves, such is its form:

Of pleurisy cautery.
The ancients said that for pleurisy, one should make cauteries of aristolochia roots in the following manner: take a long aristolochia root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and as thick and as long as your finger; and moisten it in oil and hold it over the fire and cauterize one cautery between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small cauteries slightly descending on the part that is below the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, declining a little behind; and one in the middle of the breast, and one on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on the sides of the breast outside the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but do it openly as if you were smelling.
And some of the ancients said that certain people use a fire cautery similar to a razor, and they heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; and if this is done correctly, the pain will leave as we have said in the abscess of the liver. But in this work there is fear that the patient may die or a fistula may form which cannot be healed.
of the mouse (or "mice")
When you treat the disease of the mouse (or "mice") with the methods we have mentioned in the divisions of treatments, and it does not help at all, then there are three kinds of cautery that are all good.
One of these methods consists of making three or four cauteries in a row along the length of the mouse (or "mice"), following the shape of the liver cautery that we mentioned earlier. And do not press too hard with your hand on all the cautery, and let the patient lie on their back.
And another method of cautery is to heat the cautery that has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder. And lift the curve (or "arch") that is near the mouse (or "mice"), where the patient's ribs come towards the left, and the lifting of the curve should be according to the shape of the curve, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries should be according to the width of the body.
After insert the two heated nerves until the core is pierced from the other side, then pull out the cautery, and in this way there will be four; and if you see, so cauterize with the entire cautery on three nerves. Afterward, heal when it has ejected pus for a long time, and this is worth more than the other cures mentioned before.

of the fleshy substance which is called "teat" (or "nipple")
When you cut the teat (nipple), heat up the cautery which resembles a razor, and then place it completely burning on the cut teat; and leave your hand in this position until the cautery reaches the base of the vein, causing the blood to flow out. Do this once or twice, and if there are many teats, cauterize each one as we have said. Afterwards cure them with dressings until they heal. And if you cauterize with a large cautery on alum, it will be of greater help.
of an improperly healed wound
When the patient cannot endure the work of a cutter or surgeon, which we will tell in its place, such a disease has come that it can only be healed by cautery.
When a fistula comes to someone, and it is festering and casting off corrupt moisture, you should probe it with a fine probe, and make sure that you know the depth of the entire probe. Afterwards, heat the cautery which looks like a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the length that the probe has entered, and continue heating the cautery until the decayed and corrupt flesh is burned away, one time, or two or three times, according to the amount of flesh needing to be burned; and take care not to burn the nerves which are within, and the large veins. If the fistula reaches towards the body of the bladder and intestines, then take care with those areas, and do not make incisions outside of the fleshy parts, and keep in mind that it is not a persistent [infection]; after curing the area until it is healed, if the area becomes raised and the matter has been removed for a long time, then know that the area is fully healed; but if the matter has not been removed, then know that the area is rotten, and the bones are corrupted at their base; and thus one of these [infections] which we will speak of in its place.

of the hip pain When pain comes to the hip joint and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient is treated for this as we have said in the division but the treatment is unsuccessful and the illness is old: then you must purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills or other similar good-working pills.

And if you wish, then cauterize it with the circular cautery that we mentioned earlier for the dislocation of the boil; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire boil, and all the thickness of the flesh is burnt.
And this is the method used in sciatica, when the pain is located in the hip and does not reach down to the thigh or leg. And if it reaches the thigh and the leg, then two cauteries are performed where the patient indicates that the pain is, and one cautery above the ankle four fingers wide, slightly to the left; and let the cauteries be knife-shaped, and let all the flesh be burnt; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the bones of the foot or near them, then cauterize it there where they feel the pain with three or four points using the cautery called "points".
And if necessary, then more may be done; and if they know that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then perform cautery using the knife-shaped or circular cautery, and take great care in all your cauteries that you do not leave the cautery on for too long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more harm and contraction.
And I myself have seen several who had cautery applied to the ankle of the foot, and they let it heal for so long that the leg swelled completely, and the foot as well, and the whole foot became pierced and corrupted. After which they died from a stomach complaint.

of the back pain
When pain comes to the back, either from falling, or from impact, or from excessive evacuation, or from spread out cold matter, none of these similar things is suitable for cauterization, except for that which comes from an infusion of cold matter.
It is necessary that after the patient has been purged with fetid pills or other similar things, three lines be signed on the back, in the place where the pain is located, using ink; and in each line, five cauteries or more should be made according to the potency and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cautery be made in the shape called "poins"; and if you wish, make three or four cauteries at the middle clavicle in this form:
This illness often comes to young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a stiff neck when they get up, and fear; and you will find in the lower spine of the back and the appearance which comes upon the other spines.
When you see this and wish to cure it, then cauterize it with the cautery of this sort according to this form.
So that the cautery reaches every part of the spine evenly. And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the cautery pointing two or three lines away, and let the points be close to one another. Afterward, cure the area until it is healed, as we have said, and be careful not to apply cautery to gout that is in a swollen nerve.
Of joint pain.
When there is joint pain due to moisture that has spread to all members of the body, and when pain occurs in the feet, which physicians call "gout" properly, and when it comes from a cold cause and cannot be cured by medicines, then it can be cured by cauterization in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped in this form:
And if it is necessary to cauterize the sole of the foot, let the cautery be done with a pointed instrument. And if the pains come up to the knee and other joints, which happens often, let three or four cauteries be made on each knee on every side, in an olive shape; and if you need more, do so, but do not keep your hand far from the heat of the fire.[1](note: )
And if the pains descend down to the knee and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist two lines deep; and if there remains no pain in the fingers, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the ankles or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care for the patient and give medicine. For if you take good care of them and purge fluids, they will be healed with the help of God.
Of the opening of an abscess.
When an abscess comes to a head and the intestines descend to the hips and it is recent, then when you see it needs to be cured, they must not eat that day; and they should use things that lighten the belly so that the feces come out of their stomach. Afterwards make them sit on their back between your hands and command them to hold their breath until the abscess has been retracted, and massage it with your fingers, and apply pressure underneath the opening above the bone of the wrist, and in a straight line that is half the size of a circle above the body. Then heat up the cautery iron until it is red hot, which looks like this: [The text includes a symbol for fire or the cautery iron.]
...until it turns white and drips pus. Then massage the intestines back into place, and the caregiver should place their hand to ensure that they do not move back. And work well on the thighs of the patient, and place a cushion underneath them, and a sergeant on top of the thighs, and another on the chest who holds the hands. Then apply the cautery iron on the mark with all your might, holding it directly and strongly until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, try again until you do; but carefully watch that the abscess does not burst during this process and burns neither the patient nor anyone else.
And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless. And it is necessary that the cauteries for children be fine, according to the measure of eggs, and also large for large people, according to their measure; after three days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the heat is removed; after cure with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie down for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be left on for a long time, so that the buboes do not burst when he takes a mind to move around in chambers.
And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, prepare a well-made belt for him and let him wear it for another forty days; and let him have good rest, that he does not exert himself much and guards against excessive consumption of drink and food, and of too loud laughter; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed. of old pain in some limb When pain comes to a limb, either from falling or from injury, and this pain lasts for a long time, and medical treatment is of no use, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the "point" cautery. And let the cautery be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, and power, and its location, taking into account twisting and pain. If it heals from the first cautery, that is good; but if not, begin another cautery on top of it, for sometimes it is necessary for it to change to the member that is near it, so you must continue with the cauteries until the patient is healed.
of leprosy.
Lepers are sometimes helped by cautery with great benefit, and also the diseases that come from the putrefaction of fluids and melancholy. When you see it necessary to cauterize, pay attention if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and does not worsen or remain, and you doubt that the corruption may spread throughout the patient's body, then make five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the head, and another towards the front at the end of the hair; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the nape; and leave your hand so that the cautery reaches the bone, and so much that the scabs come out, allowing the vapors of the gross humors to escape; and cauterize the area according to what it is before.
And if the sickness is spread everywhere and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize it with the cauteries that we have mentioned in the head, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the haunch and another next to it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the ribs, and two on the groins of the chest, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are at the back of the heels; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one on the bone of the stomach, and one on the liver.
And know that the more cautery you do, the more help you provide, and it benefits them; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because their body is already completely corrupted. And it is necessary for the cautery to be large or small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the forms of irons. After the cure, sprinkle the wound with barley flour and honey and other cures until it is healed.

When swelling comes to any limb and is treated by medicines, oils, and plasters, but it is not healed, then cauterization is done on the limb according to the size of the member; and let the cautery be a little deep in the flesh; then cure it with ointments until it is healed. And sometimes cauterization is done on the hand, foot, and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed; but no one should interfere if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the moving nerves of the body.

When the disease called "albaras" has woken up and the means of medicine are worth nothing, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the amount of flesh, until the whiteness is removed and the color changed; then cure it with bran of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of dove and almond, each one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and expose it to air until it is healed.
The treatment of chancre (a type of skin ulcer) with cautery involves using a hot iron or other heated instrument to burn and destroy the infected tissue. This was a common medical practice in the Middle Ages as it was believed to remove the corrupt humors and promote healing. After cauterization, the wound would be cleaned and dressed with various medicinal substances such as herbs, oils, and powders to help prevent infection and promote healing. The specific method of cautery used for chancre may have varied depending on the severity of the ulcer and the practitioner's preference.
When a chancre begins to appear, and you wish to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the circumference of the chancre. And yet, wise men say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, for I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen several times; and a more appropriate thing is that it be cauterized around, with the "circular" cautery, as we have said in many cauteries.
of the swelling that cannot spread
When someone has a disease called "adubelati," and it delays in healing, either because of the superfluity that it makes or because of the water of the sick person when they are infirm (that is to say, too old) and have little blood, or for time; and you wish to hasten its healing: then cauterize it all around with many small cauteries by pricking; after leave it as such. For it will hurry to heal.
And if you wish to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery like this: [shape of the cautery is not provided in the text].
And place your hand in the middle of the ailment called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced through to the heart, and make the cauteries such that the patient feels them from outside in such a way that the course of the putrefaction is alleviated. Afterward heal it until it is perfectly healed.
the healing by fire using iron
There is another kind of illness called "corrodens", which is nothing but an eating away of the limbs, just like fire consumes dry wood. If you see this illness in a place that can bear cautery with fire, then heat up the cauteries, both large and small, according to what is needed for the location where the illness is; after that, cauterize all around until you reach all of the corruption, and let nothing of it remain. Then leave it alone for three days, and put soothing ointment on the cauterized areas with oil until the burns from the fire are healed, and all of the corruption. Afterward, heal with ointments that generate flesh. And if you see after three days that healthy flesh is not born, this is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupted areas. This eating away has sometimes been cured by soothing medicine instead of cautery with fire, but still, cautery with fire is of greater help, and I have already said the cure for soothing medicine in the division: take as much as you need when you require it.
of fungi that come between the toes
Very often, a disease arises in the feet, which we call "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large abscess that wounds the foot. And the cautery for this disease is of two kinds: namely, fire cautery and hot water cautery. The fire cautery is as follows: heat a red-hot iron rod as thin as a pen, made of good metal and of a size that can reach the root of the ababscess from all sides, with sharp edges; then place it very hot on the abscess, turning your hand around the rod until you reach the base of the abscess; leave it there for three days until it begins to rot; then apply a plaster made of crushed unripe grapes with oil, and leave it overnight; the pus will come out and the rod will be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the wound by cleaning away any rotten flesh until it is healed.
And if they (abscesses) are located in various parts of the body, and this happens often in hands and feet, then you should use hot water cautery; and it is done in this manner: take a rod of iron or copper, or a pen-shaped instrument, and place the red-hot tip on the abscess, that is to say, powdered verdigris (a medicinal compound); then place the rod so that it surrounds (the abscess) completely, then add some hot water and hold your hand firmly, pressing down while turning so that the edges of the rod come into contact with the root of the abscess and can find a path through the heat to reach the root; allow the patient to endure the biting heat of the water for a while (about an hour); then leave it be and it will detach itself, along with all its roots. Do this repeatedly until all the ones in the body have been treated in this way, then cure the wounds by cleaning away any rotten flesh.
The treatment for trembling.
When someone is trembling from cold nerves or quartan fever or any other cause, then you should apply four or five cauteries to them on the spine at the base of the neck, one cautery between each vertebra; and one cautery on the affected area (pez) and one on the stomach using an olive-shaped cautery. This will stop the trembling and speed up recovery from the cold disease.[br]
of stinking pustules
Sometimes appear on the body, due to negligence, stinking pustules that come from corrupt matter. In this case, it is necessary, at first when they appear, to make a cautery on each head of the pustule: with a subtle cautery made from myrtle wood, whose tip is taken by fire, or from a long aristolochia root, or with a round cautery. And sometimes they are cauterized in the beginning, when they appear, in this manner, and they cannot grow any further, but rather the superfluities from which they come are broken up, and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
when an artery is cut. It often happens that there is a large loss of blood from the artery that is cut in an injury or incision of an abscess, or in the cauterization of a limb, and similar things; and it is very difficult to stop the bleeding.
And yet, when this happens to someone, you must quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein and press very hard until the bleeding stops under your finger and no more blood comes out; then heat various sized olive-shaped cauters over the fire until they are all red; then apply one, large or small according to the wound and the location where the artery is cut, and place the cauter on that vein where you have your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding stops.
And if it jumps out when you lift your hand above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take another cautery quickly from the fire.
And do not cease to do this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is next to it, and ensure no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be easily stopped, especially when the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways we have mentioned: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not yet treated, or by tightly binding with a bandage, or by medicines placed on it that have the power to stop blood; and it should be bound and held in place.
Whoever will attempt to stop the bleeding by tightly binding with bandages or placing hot objects on it, or similar things, will not succeed if it is not effective.[Reference(s):
And if this happens to someone and they do not have medicine or mirrors present, then they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and press down firmly until it stops bleeding above the wound and above the vein; and they must not move it, but wet it frequently with very cold water until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped; and make preparations in advance for what they need of cauteries and medicines.
We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or burning medicine, and we have described the operations, causes, instruments, and forms of cauteries; and I have placed the chapter on head wounds at the beginning up to feet, and I will go in this chapter along the same path so that one may more easily find what one wants.
And so, as I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you know that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter of cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
And I warn you not to undertake foolish things. For many kinds of people come to be treated, some of whom are so afraid of their illness that they easily die from the violence they find in their disease and the severity of its malice; and one should fear these people. And of these, there are some who claim to be healed and say: "wait, I am healed"; and the disease is contemptuous. It is not at all appropriate for you to agree to those who come to you with this attitude, but rather put more effort into your honor than into your greed, and do not rashly but wisely open up those from whom you are certain, and from whom you can gain credit and praise; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients for their health to be restored; and this will help you establish a good reputation, and glory, and memories of praise.
Dear son, may Our Lord grant you good understanding and justice, and if you wish to inspire yourself with the holy inspiration of his hand, Amen.
And so I have organized this chapter by topics, as it is before the chapter on cauteries that I have described from head to toe, so that you may more easily find what you need.

for stopping up ears
All that falls in ears is one of four things: grains or animals, stone from mines or similar things such as iron; or seeds such as pus, beans, peas; or liquids such as water and earwax and similar things.
When it falls into the ear a stone or any other thing that does not join with the ear, nor grows in the ear, place the ear in the sun. If you see the stone, distill a drop of violet oil or oil of cedar, then attempt extraction; and make him sneeze using drugs, and stop up his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear upward. This cure often works; and if it does not work, attempt extraction using subtle tweezers, of which this is the shape:
If it comes out with the tweezers, that is good; if not, attempt extraction using a thin wire hook; and if it does not come out this way either, then make a small silver tube and insert the end of the tube into the ear hole, and stop up the area around the tube with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the tube; then pull it out strongly, for often it comes out as we have said; and if it does not come out in this manner, take birdlime with which birds are caught, and place some on an instrument made for this purpose, and put a piece of cotton around; then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out. And if it does not come out with all the things we have mentioned, then quickly make an incision in the ear so that abscess and callus may not form, and spasms; and the manner of the incision should be such that you first bleed the patient from the head, and draw blood according to their strength, then have the patient sit between your hands and turn their ear upward, and make a small incision at the base of the ear in the fatty area; and let the incision be like a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then remove it as best you can, and quickly suck on it with your mouth; and continue this treatment until it has healed. And if it is a grain that is inside and has become swollen, then attempt extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a thin probe according to this shape:
and make an incision on that swelling. But do not do so when you think that the swelling is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with delicate tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
And in the case of water that falls into the ear, the patient should use sneezing with previous conditions, and widen the ear with soft cotton. And lie on that same ear where the water is. If it comes out by this means, it is good. If not, take many small and light pebbles, and heat them a little in the fire; and put one of these stones into the patient's ear, and jump on the other side, and strike another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this with stone after stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will come out completely; and if you see, take a reed, and put one end into the ear, and light the other end with fire until the thickest part of the reed is burned; then do the same thing again with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said with the stone.
In the extraction of an animal, if it has a small body, such as a flea and similar things, cure it as we have said in division; but if it is of large size that can be felt, then make an extraction with tweezers; and this is one of the easiest things to remove from the ear.

And let it be tight down below and wide above. And insert the slenderest tip into the ear according to the severity of the patient's pain, then pull the entire canal strongly; do this frequently until all the worms come out. And if they do not obey in coming out, then stop up around the canal with cotton as I have said in the previous passage; and if they still do not come out as we have mentioned, then administer the infusions that the ancients have tested in cases of worms, which you will find in the treatment of infusions; and then distill your oils and medicines into the ear using this instrument, such is the method as you see.

on the stoppage of ears
No child is born who does not have any holes in their ears; and the same thing happens to adults through blockage from wounds or flesh grown inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes occur deep within the ear where they cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a pouch visible outside the hole.
Then, the one that comes deep, if it cannot be seen, is of difficult healing in many ways; and in the one that can be seen, it is necessary that you place the sick person's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the swelling apparent, work on it immediately with this instrument, according to its shape.
And let it be sharp and blunt at the front and back, so that it does not wound the ear; if the swelling is in the flesh or core of the ear, hold it with delicate pincers and cut lightly, until all the flesh is removed.
And if the swelling is deep within the ear, take a delicate and sharp lancet, heat it slightly by the fire, then place it in the core of the ear. If you feel the swelling, which causes pain for the patient upon hearing, make a small puncture but be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then insert into the ear a wick according to the width of the opening and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Do this for several days until the wound heals or take a wick and moisten it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on top; and if you see the ear swelling, then you must remove the wick and replace it with another one moistened in an ointment made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then continue to care for it until it is healed.
And if flowing of blood occurs, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other cures that stop the flow of blood, which are in the treatment of distillations.
The translation of "de la char des papieres" would be "of the pulp of paper".
This eye-salve that comes in paper, when it is moist and dry, you should stretch it with tongs and forceps, and cut off a piece of its roots with a spatula; then put vitriol powder on the spot.
And if blood flows from it (the eye), cauterize it with a subtle circular cautery, and then the cauterizer should move the incision; and many times they (the eyes) recover, as long as anything remains of their roots; and when they are burned by fire, those roots are destroyed and do not return.
The translation of "de la gresle" is "of hail". This term is used to describe a medical condition caused by hailstorms. In medieval medicine, it was believed that being caught in a hailstorm could cause injury or illness, and specific remedies were recommended for treating these conditions. The text you provided describes the use of a cautery to treat an eye affected by a hailstorm.

of eye ulceration
When this disease called "aleacrati" or ulceration occurs in the eye, it can be of two types: one natural and the other unnatural. It can happen suddenly due to a wound, a cut, or a burn, and similar things.[note]Aleacrati is not a known medical term in modern medicine. However, based on the context, it could refer to an eye condition characterized by some kind of ulceration or inflammation.[/note]
The method of treatment for this condition is to lance the abscess, separate its lips, and place inside linen bandages, keeping them in place until it has healed. It is important that you do not use drying or constricting substances in the treatment. If you do, the condition will return worse than before. Instead, use softening agents such as fenugreek; and boil linseed, barley, and linseed oil, add powdered dyallium and heat it in one of the oils, then wrap it in a bandage and treat the eye with it.[note]Dyallium is an antimony compound that was used as a medication in the Middle Ages. It was often used as a diuretic and to treat skin conditions such as ulcers, ringworm, and lice.[/note][Note: The modern medical term for this condition is likely to be different from "aleacrati" or eye ulceration, as these terms are not used in contemporary medicine. If you have concerns about your eyes or any symptoms you are experiencing, it's important to consult a healthcare professional for an accurate diagnosis and treatment plan.]
And the treasure of your care is that you ensure it does not heal according to the shape it was before; and these works that we have mentioned are none except remedies for this disease, so that it does not heal according to the shape it was before.
of the flesh that comes to the eye
This disease which is under the eye, which is truly called "axacrati," and it is natural as well as accidental. "De l'ungle de l'oeil" means "of the eyelid." The eyelid is a protective flap of skin that covers and protects the eye. It helps to keep the eye moist by spreading tears over the surface of the eye, and it also helps to prevent foreign objects from entering the eye. In medical texts, the eyelid may be referred to as the "palpebra" or "lid." The phrase "de l'ungle de l'oeil" specifically refers to the edge or margin of the eyelid where it meets the eyeball. This area is particularly important for maintaining the health and function of the eye, as it helps to distribute tears and protect the eye from foreign objects. In some medical procedures, the eyelid may need to be treated or manipulated in order to address issues with the eye itself.

This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but the bow formed in the eye, appearing like descending water, and it's not actually water; and one way to recognize its appearance is to have the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then hold their head with both of your hands and move it until you see the bow come up to your eyes; then stick it in place and let the light not go down and let the patient see things as they used to; and if it doesn't descend, know that it is water, and if the descent of the bow is not prepared as we have said, make the patient sit between your hands, then take a fine spatula and push on the transparent cornea through the continuation of the conjunctiva with the transparent cornea and the crown until the bow comes out; and when it has come out, distill warm water mixed with honey, or boiled water and honey, into the eye, then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
of the waters (or fluids) of the eye
We have similar instances of the waters (or fluids) in division, and what is required for piercing; and we work according to health. If the water descends now, let the patient look before him and the instrument in his eye.

of the flesh from (the) nose
Sometimes different kinds of flesh are born on the nose, among which there are some that resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are such ones that have fleshy growths of a violet color, and they also have soft flesh of good color. In this case, of these two kinds of flesh, if it is soft and not swollen, you should make the patient sit between your hands in front of the sun; and clear their nostrils, and pour the eye ointment on those fleshy growths, and pull them out; then cut what you can hold with a sharp spatula from one side, until you are certain that all the flesh is removed.
And if there remains any part that cannot be cut, open it with a very fine and light instrument so that nothing remains; and if pus forms or an abscess arises, treat it as necessary; and if they are malignant abscesses, cauterize it quickly to stop the bleeding and remove all the flesh; then pour rosewater, vinegar, or wine on (the nose).
If the nose does not drain and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healed; but if the moisture does not drain as it should, know that flesh has grown in the bone above, which the instruments cannot reach. In this case, you must insert a fairly thick linen thread and tie it loosely with small knots at intervals of about one digit or less; then place the thread in the patient's nose to the best of their ability, and pull on it while sniffing until it comes through the nose into the mouth. This is something that many children in school do, and it is not difficult for those who want to do it. Then hold the piece of flesh coming out of the nose with one hand, and the piece coming out of the mouth with the other hand, and know which knot has touched the rotten flesh. Continue this until you are sure that the knots have destroyed all the flesh, then remove the thread, wipe away the blood, moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment, and replace it in the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has dissolved all remaining flesh. Then place a piece of wax in the nose for several days until it is healed; and if drying medicines are needed, use them. This is the form of the instrument for purging the head, with which oils and medicines are distilled into the nose.

of flesh from the nose
Often a sickness is born in the head of the nose, called "telul", and it grows and becomes large at times, to the point where it is visible; and therefore you must cut it at the beginning and extract it all, then place on it the cautery or a burning medicine; and if you wait until it has grown large before cutting it, see if it is hard, of a dark color, with little sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, because when it is cut once, it can cause great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of a dark color, and you see that you can extract all of it, have the patient empty their stomach and cauterize the area without fear, and cure it with drying and constricting agents.

abscesses of the lips

of the flesh of the gums
Often, a swelling of the flesh occurs on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with tongs and cut it at its root, letting the pus or blood run out; then put vitriol powder or other restraining and desiccative powders on the wound; and if this flesh comes back after the incision, which often happens, you should cut it again and cauterize it; it will not come back after cauterization. of deafness
Sometimes, calluses appear on the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth become black, green, and yellow, such that the corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul-smelling; you should make the patient sit between your hands, with their chin in your holy palm, and scrape the visible calluses or teeth until nothing remains; and similarly for any black, green, or yellow stains, as well as for any other discolorations, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is present at the first cleaning, that is good; if not, then start again on the second and third day, continuing to scrape until everything is removed. And know that teeth require various forms of instruments for scraping, according to what the work demands, because the scrapers used to scrape outside the teeth have different shapes than those used between the teeth; these forms and others should be prepared in advance.
When you cure a toothache, you must delay pulling the tooth as long as possible, because one should not do it hastily; for it is a very serious matter until there is no excuse to pull (the tooth). Then when the patient is ready to pull, you should make sure of the decayed tooth. Often it happens that the pain deceived the patient, and he thinks it is in a healthy tooth, and has a good tooth pulled; yet the pain does not go away, for the bad tooth remains, as we have often seen with surgeons; and when you are certain of the decayed tooth, you should cauterize around the tooth with a strong styptic to protect the gum from all sides; then pull it out with your hands or with fine tweezers, pulling firmly at first and then more gently until it is completely loose; then securely clamp the tweezers; and have the patient's head between your knees, holding it firmly so that it does not move.
After pulling the tooth out straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and gently push it in on both sides, and move it as you did before. And if the teeth are rotten or crumbled, you must fill them with cloth where the holes are; and clamp them delicately with tweezers, so that they do not break when clamped; and you must work very carefully around the gum to loosen the tooth.
And take care not to break it and leave a part in the patient's mouth, causing greater pain than the original through the malice of the root. Also, be careful not to act as ignorant surgeons do, who sometimes out of haste and recklessness break the jaw, without achieving what we have described; but instead bring about great illness from the roots that remain or from the broken jaw, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, rinse the area with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply a vitriol paste; and if that does not work, cauterize the wound.

When the front teeth loosen, either from a blow or a fall, and the patient cannot chew food without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines without success, then they must be constricted with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to realign the teeth, take the thread and pass it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the loose teeth on the thread, if there is one or more, until you come to a healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering again up to the point where you started, and gently but firmly pull your hand until it does not move; and let your grip be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the teeth free with pliers and align them, and place them between the healthy tooth and the loose one, and position them so as not to injure the tongue; and then leave them as tight as they can endure, and if they loosen or the wire breaks, then constrict them with another wire; if they remain in place, it will serve them for their entire lifetime, and this is the method for aligning two loose teeth and two healthy ones, as you see.
And when a tooth falls out, it is replaced in its place as soon as possible, as we have said; and one should not meddle with it unless they are wise and skilled; and sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from animal bone, and it is placed in the gap where it is needed, and it is constricted as we have said, and it remains in place for a long time.
to cut the tie of the tongue
Sometimes there is a ligament underneath the tongue, which is natural and present at birth, or it can be due to an accidental closure of a wound; and the procedure is as follows: open the patient's mouth, hold their head in your hands, and lift their tongue. Then cut the nervous ligament widely, so that the tongue is loosened from its anchorage, and if there is any hardness or knot, which is due to a sudden wound, insert the hook and cut it widely. Be careful not to make the incision too deep, as there is an artery underneath. After you have done this, apply a swab of rose water and vinegar, or cold water, then place a linen bandage under the tongue. The patient should change the bandage every night, to prevent reattachment. If bleeding occurs, apply a mixture of vitriol, and if the wound does not heal, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this purpose. Finally, treat the wound with other treatments until it heals completely.[INTUITIVE AI] The text describes a medical procedure for treating a ligament under the tongue that may be present since birth or caused by an accidental injury. of abscesses in the throat
