Here's the translation of "de la cuixe brisie" from Old French to English:
The thigh bone is often broken, and it's easily noticeable when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration consists of tying one bandage above the fracture, and another below it. And the patient lies on his back, then each assistant stretches out their rope evenly on their side; and that is when the fracture is between the bones.
And if the fracture is near the thigh root, let one of the ropes be towards the wrist, and the other ropes below the fracture. And similarly if it is near the knee, and then let the rope be next to the knee, and the extension downwards; then let the physician put the bone even with his two hands, until it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the poultice and bandage, if pus does not form.
And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside first and then return to your work and care; the bandage is done in such a way. It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture a hard bandage doubled in two or three layers, and let the extra material remain, then bend the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg next to the knee below, and make the ends of the thread come up; then wrap around the leg and thigh the bandage, then place splints on the fracture, and place one splint on the bone of the leg; then apply a soft dressing between the thigh and leg made of soft cloths to keep the tension even, then begin to tightly bind three or four turns around the fracture; and as you go up the fracture, tighten less; then pay attention to the two ends of the thread that you put between the leg and thigh, and tie them with the three splints that are above, then return to the underside of the thread end, until you come next to the foot; and tighten it so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, unless there comes a abscess or swelling or other similar thing.
And if it happens, loosen it, and realign what is coming out, as we have said many times; and if there are fragments of the bone that prick, they must be gouged out if possible; and if not, the place must be broken open and pulled out; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
And sometimes the hip is broken so that steel pins are put in, as in the shoulder and arm; yet, with this kind of restoration, the patient does not fare well.
And know that the hip is restored in 30 days, or a little less or a little more, according to the differences in constitutions.
of the groin of the knee
Know that in the hollow of the knee there often occurs a small break, but it bends many times. And if it breaks, it is only a crack or a hole, and it happens with all wounds, with or without wound, and this one can feel well.
And the restoration is that one sets even what is dislocated at its joints, so that it can be moved as soon as possible; then applies the poultice and places a round bandage if necessary, and binds it as needed. Then consider all the precautions as we have mentioned in other fractures, such as hot abscess and similar things; and for each symptom, do what is necessary, until it is healed.
of the fracture of the leg

And if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns all around.
And if the small bones are broken, it turns forward.
And if the large bone is broken, there is great pain and it is visible; and it turns upside down. Then provide traction, align it properly, and bind the splints evenly. of the fracture of the leg bones
At the ankle, there is never a break, but sometimes a break occurs in the bones of the foot and toes, and it only results in a fracture in multiple positions.
If there is a break in the bones of the foot and you see the bones sticking out, place the patient's foot on the ground as if they were going to walk, then place your foot on top of theirs where the bones are protruding, and press down until they return to their place. Then apply a poultice and bandages, and place a small board with two flat chips under the belly of the foot, and bind it to the foot with wraps and other necessary items.
And when three or four days have passed, loosen the binding because you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.[*Note: I translated "desaluez" as dislocated, but it can also mean displaced or out of alignment.*]
And if some of the toes are broken, then set them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; and for the broken toe, place a splint the length of the toe, and make it slightly wider, then place the board that I mentioned under the foot and bind it in place. If there are two or three, or more, broken toes, then place a splint on each one according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board under the foot; and let it be placed above the belly of the foot so that it touches it well.[*Note: I translated "defuer" as above, but it can also mean over or outside.*]
And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, just as we have mentioned; and treat each accident as it should be.
of the fracture of the arm bone (radius/ulna)
When the bone of a woman's body is broken, make her sit with her legs spread apart, then lean her back towards the part of her spine and have someone hold her from behind; next, fill a cloth bag with cotton and put in it as much as a finger's width; then stand the woman up and lift her hips and buttocks, and the cotton will come out until it reaches the opening of the body, and the bone will return to its place with the finger's width; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has finished urinating, put it back in, and do this for seven days or so: her fracture will be healed. And if you want, take a bladder of a sheep and attach a pipe to its opening, and insert the entire bladder into the body; then blow hard into the pipe until the bladder is filled inside: the bone will return to its place. Then fill it with cotton and leave it like that for several days until it heals.
And when the arm bone of a man or woman is broken, restore it in the same way as we have said for the thigh bone; and these fractures are not hidden from one who applies their effort and skill, and pays attention to my book. For fractures indicate in many ways the correct path of restoration: pay attention then.
In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose gullet and insert the penis in it; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or until it heals quickly.
of fracture with wound
It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that it be healed now, so that the bleeding which we have mentioned testifies to this.[NOTE: I made an assumption that "sainies" refers to bleeding. If there are any other possible meanings for this word in the context of medieval medical texts, please let me know.]
And if the wound is healed, then stain it with vitriol (sulfuric acid), if you have nothing else; then begin to treat the fracture in that same hour or on that day, unless abscesses come.
And if abscesses come, then leave the treatment for nine days until the abscess subsides, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, because you would bring about an evil outcome there.[NOTE: I made an assumption that "li apostemes" refers to abscesses or pus-filled swellings. If there are any other possible meanings for this word in the context of medieval medical texts, please let me know.]
And if the broken bone appears under the skin, it is necessary to put it back in place gently with your hands, with slight extension.
And if the extension is not suitable for you to put it equal with your hands, then use this iron instrument that is 7 or 8 fingers long, and its width corresponds to the size of the wound; and it is necessary for the surgeon to prepare 3 or 4 (fingers), according to what is needed in each bone-breaking treatment; and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not bend during compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp in front, and thick from the middle forward, like this:
And it is called "palancelle," for which reason the curved head should be placed on the surface of the visible bone; and push it once until it aligns, and make sure they are even with each other. And if the fracture is subtle and the instrument cannot grasp the bone well, then you must cut the end of the bone so that the instrument has enough power to hold it.
And if you cannot realign the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, such as a chisel or knife, to your best ability; and then remove any roughness and small fragments from the bone.
And when the bone is set back in place, and the patient still feels great pain, know that it is not in its natural position. Make sure it is in its correct position, then wet a cloth in stypic black wine, and apply it properly if it's during summer; and do not put any ointment or other things with oil on the wound, as it may cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer painkillers when you have set the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, cutting away the cover as needed around the wound, taking care that the wound is not constricted by the broken bones; for many foolish surgeons have caused either death or infection in the patient by making the restraints too tight; and the restraints should be looser and more gentle than other types of breaks.
And if the wound is large or deep, and you fear that complications may arise, as we have mentioned, and you find pain in the area, then it is not appropriate to apply painkillers; instead, wrap hard bandages around the wound, in place of painkillers, and bind them. After one day or two, if you see pus forming on the wound, remove what you have placed on it and apply a wound-healing ointment, such as tetrafarmaçon or similar.
And it is necessary to unbind the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it has healed and become clean.
And it is necessary that the limb be equipped in such a way that the pus drains easily.
And if for many days they are exceedingly weak, and it can no longer heal but keeps breaking open, know that there are small pieces of bone, therefore you should stitch the wound with sutures, and remove all the separated pieces that cause the pain.
And if a fistula comes to the place, or any other form of corruption, then you should treat it, according to what is said in its chapter earlier. And when the bone is broken and apparent on the limb, such as the bones of the thigh or the shoulder, and similar parts of large members, do not pull it out, because many times death results from this; but let it be until it rots; perhaps it will come out after 20 or 30 days. Then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
swellings that come upon sutures
We often see after the healing of a fracture, even when it is close to the joint, and it results in an unsightly appearance of the limb; and perhaps the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Take great care then if it is fresh to us: administer styptic medicines to him, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others, so that you take some of these things, or all together, and cook them with astringent wine or with egg yolk or with vinegar; and put it on the wound in lint, and bind it well, and do not loosen it for several days; and then loosen, and begin another, until the knot is removed; or you strain on a piece of wood well made; for the property of wood is that it removes all swellings above the members; and if the knot has already turned into hardness like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, then cut it off, and let the excess appear; or you have it scraped by a skilled barber, until it is removed, and cure it until it is healed.
When the fracture of the bone has healed, but the limb remains weak and fine afterwards, it happens for many reasons: one of which is that it was tied too tight, and not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and the nourishment could not reach the member; or due to an excess of moisture; or due to excessive movements, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in its body, so it is weak.
And the cure is to make the patient eat, and make the body supple, so that the blood is multiplied in him; and administer baths for him, and give him joy and pleasure; then apply a poultice to the limb, so that the poultice draws great nourishment to it, and often moisten it with warm water, until the nourishment reaches the member; and it regains its natural appearance.
of the crooked member after the healing
When the member is crooked after restoration, and the broken bone is clearly visible, and the shape of the member is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function; do not believe the foolish ones who say that the member must be broken again, and many foolish surgeons have done this in our land; and these works are blamed, and great harm comes from them, and perhaps death; however, if the nodes and swelling are fresh, they should be soaked in hot water or softening herbs should be cooked, such as leaves of mallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, such as well-made cerate, and take the marshmallow root, and cook it with goose fat or oil of St. John's wort, and make a plaster with it; or take fat figs, and crush them with cow dung, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
And sometimes the nodes are removed by continuous and prolonged rubbing with wet hands. And let there be gentle movement of the member every hour.
And if the crookedness is old and hardened, like stone, and it needs to be removed with iron, then it should be covered up to the bone with a subtle incision, lightly and skillfully; and cotton and bandages should be used in the care of the wound.
Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocation arises from a joint being out of its place, causing the limb to be misaligned and the patient to feel great pain and injury.
When a dislocation occurs, it must be corrected immediately.
For if one waits, the area swells and it may be difficult to reset it later; therefore, it is not advisable to move it when it is swollen, as this can cause spasms and other pains.
Nevertheless, when this occurs, let the patient be bled, then allow time for the abscess to subside; then apply warm water and oil to the affected limb, gently reset it, and treat each limb as it returns to its place
And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations of the joints from head to foot.
of the jaws
It is rare for both jaws to be dislocated, and there are two ways in which this dislocation can occur: either they are slightly pulled out of their place and somewhat relaxed; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the back, causing saliva to flow from the mouth that the person cannot hold in, nor can they close their mouth, and their tongue is enveloped by their speech.
When the dislocation is small, it will return to its place through several positions.
And if it is complete and full, you must quickly reset it and not delay.
And in such a way that the attendant holds the head of the patient, and with one of his hands puts his finger into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two-parted; and let the other hand be free to adjust and align; and command the patient to relax and move their jaw in all directions.
And the physician adjusts it evenly, until it returns to its place.
And if the returning (of the jaw) is difficult, even if it's both mandibles together, soak them with warm water and oil, until you can gently adjust them; do not delay the adjustment, as we have said.
And when they are evenly adjusted and the patient's mouth closes well without force, then place wet bandages soaked in a mixture of rose oil and wax on it, and gently bind it with soft ligatures.
and let the patient sleep on their back, with their heels resting between two cushions, so that they do not move it to the right or left, nor should they strive to increase the pain, but should eat light food until the pains are eased, and the jaw joints are relaxed.
and then let them eat what they want, but lightly, and do not strain to open their mouth while eating or drinking, until the jaw joints are fully relaxed and healed.
And if the two jaw bones cannot be put back in place at once and are not returned to their proper position, fever and swelling may occur, and perhaps stomach upset, and possibly vomiting of bile.
And when you see this, know that it is a critical situation; and many times the person dies, within nine days.
of the fork/fracture
The fracture cannot come out of alignment along the ribcage and the hip, and when it is dislocated, it can be felt.
And the treatment is as follows: let the patient lie flat on their back, extend their arms, then press firmly with your palm in that area, and it will return to its proper position. Then apply a poultice and bandage, and bind it.
And the head that is turned towards the shoulder cannot come out of alignment. If it does dislocate, reset it to its proper position as we have said. Then apply a poultice and bandage, and bind it, and tell the patient to rest until they are healed.[Source: Medieval medical treatise from the 12th-13th century]
And similarly, bring the head of the shoulder back into its proper position when it has become dislocated.
of the dislocation of the shoulder
Know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways only: one of which is when it dislocates at the side of the shoulder blade below; the second is at the part of the hip; and it may happen to dislocate above, but this is rare.
and it should never dislocate backward at the shoulder blade, nor inside near the nerves; and it dislocates below towards the shoulder blade many times, especially in those who have little flesh, for it slips out quickly; but in those who have enough flesh, it slips out with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
And perhaps it happens to some men that they receive a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they believe that it is dislocated because of this.[INT](Note: I will provide you with more lines from the medieval medical treatise as soon as you are ready.)

The method is as follows: the assistant raises the patient's hand up high, then places their fingers under the shoulder blade and lifts the joint with force upwards to its proper place. then pull the foot toward you with your right hand, and then twice with your left hand, then stretch it upwards, and nicely push the foot upward;

and if it cannot return into place this way, then have the patient lie down on their back on the ground, and firmly plant a stake in the ground between their thighs and tie a cloth around it so that it does not injure the patient;

And if abscesses come from it, you should soothe it, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
of the hands
When the hand is dislocated, you should stretch it out nicely without force, and this is an easy thing to do.
And if the dislocation is in any joint of the back or foot, you should make the patient sit straight on a flat bench or on a table with their legs stretched out. Then put your foot on the exposed part of the joints and press firmly until it returns to its place.
and when it is even, and there is nothing visible, place a two-footed table under the sole of the foot, then pull hard and leave it for three days, then loosen it; and let it rest until it is healed.
of wound and dislocation together
When a wound accompanies a dislocation, and one wants to restore it, it often happens that the patient dies.
